0.0713501C10.8805 0.0614624 10.8164 0.0461426 10.7548 0.0313721ZM7.34082 7.47388C7.62811 7.2063 7.9154 6.9209 8.20269 6.6355C8.18016 6.62988 8.16114 6.62427 8.14401 6.6192C8.10655 6.60822 8.07805 6.59985 8.04109 6.59985C7.03556 6.15393 5.83253 6.3501 5.04246 7.11713C3.606 8.52625 2.1875 9.93542 0.768994 11.3624C0.14053 11.9867 -0.0928837 12.7715 0.032803 13.6277C0.194409 14.7515 0.840817 15.5184 1.9002 15.8752C2.97755 16.2319 3.94717 16.0001 4.75517 15.2152C5.6766 14.3118 6.59005 13.4004 7.50616 12.4864C7.96467 12.0289 8.42384 11.5708 8.88501 11.1127C9.56733 10.4348 9.81871 9.61432 9.67506 8.66895C9.63916 8.41925 9.56733 8.16949 9.42369 7.9198C9.13639 8.2052 8.8491 8.47272 8.57975 8.75812C8.54385 8.776 8.54385 8.84735 8.54385 8.90082C8.61567 9.41809 8.47203 9.8819 8.09495 10.2565C6.71235 11.6478 5.31181 13.0391 3.91125 14.4125C3.51623 14.8228 2.99551 14.9655 2.43889 14.8406C1.81042 14.6979 1.4154 14.3234 1.23584 13.7347C1.05629 13.1282 1.19993 12.5753 1.64882 12.1294C2.34011 11.4337 3.03141 10.747 3.72271 10.0603C4.41401 9.37354 5.10531 8.68677 5.79661 7.99115C6.17369 7.59869 6.65849 7.45599 7.19717 7.50952C7.25103 7.50952 7.3049 7.50952 7.34082 7.47388Z" fill="#808495"></path></svg></div></h3>
<p>In the sections above, we talked a lot about issues when mutating return objects of cached functions. This topic is complicated! But it&#x27;s central to understanding the behavior differences between <code>st.cache_data</code> and <code>st.cache_resource</code>. So let&#x27;s dive in a bit deeper.</p>
<p>First, we should clearly define what we mean by mutations and concurrency:</p>
<ul>
<li>
<p>By <strong>mutations</strong>, we mean any changes made to a cached function&#x27;s return value <em>after</em> that function has been called. I.e. something like this:</p>
<section class="code_Container__pq3Nr"><div class="code_Pre__3lyyf"><code class="language-python">@st.cache_data
def create_list():
    l = [1, 2, 3]

l = create_list()  # ðŸ‘ˆ Call the function
l[0] = 2  # ðŸ‘ˆ Mutate its return value
</code></div></section>
</li>
<li>
<p>By <strong>concurrency</strong>, we mean that multiple sessions can cause these mutations at the same time. Streamlit is a web framework that needs to handle many users and sessions connecting to an app. If two people view an app at the same time, they will both cause the Python script to rerun, which may manipulate cached return objects at the same time â€“ concurrently.</p>
</li>
</ul>
<p>Mutating cached return objects can be dangerous. It can lead to exceptions in your app and even corrupt your data (which can be worse than a crashed app!). Below, we&#x27;ll first explain the copying behavior of <code>st.cache_data</code> and show how it can avoid mutation issues. Then, we&#x27;ll show how concurrent mutations can lead to data corruption and how to prevent it.</p>
<h4 id="copying-behavior"><a href="/develop/concepts/architecture/caching#copying-behavior"><span class="icon icon-link"></span></a>Copying behavior</h4>
<p><code>st.cache_data</code> creates a copy of the cached return value each time the function is called. This avoids most mutations and concurrency issues. To understand it in detail, let&#x27;s go back to the <a href="/develop/concepts/architecture/caching#usage">Uber ridesharing example</a> from the section on <code>st.cache_data</code> above. We are making two modifications to it:</p>
<ol>
<li>We are using <code>st.cache_resource</code> instead of <code>st.cache_data</code>. <code>st.cache_resource</code> does <strong>not</strong> create a copy of the cached object, so we can see what happens without the copying behavior.</li>
<li>After loading the data, we manipulate the returned DataFrame (in place!) by dropping the column <code>&quot;Lat&quot;</code>.</li>
</ol>
<p>Here&#x27;s the code:</p>
<section class="code_Container__pq3Nr"><div class="code_Pre__3lyyf"><code class="language-python">@st.cache_resource   # ðŸ‘ˆ Turn off copying behavior
def load_data(url):
    df = pd.read_csv(url)
    return df

df = load_data(&quot;https://raw.githubusercontent.com/plotly/datasets/master/uber-rides-data1.csv&quot;)
st.dataframe(df)

df.drop(columns=[&#x27;Lat&#x27;], inplace=True)  # ðŸ‘ˆ Mutate the dataframe inplace

st.button(&quot;Rerun&quot;)
</code></div></section>
<p>Let&#x27;s run it and see what happens! The first run should work fine. But in the second run, you see an exception: <code>KeyError: &quot;[&#x27;Lat&#x27;] not found in axis&quot;</code>. Why is that happening? Let&#x27;s go step by step:</p>
<ul>
<li>On the first run, Streamlit runs <code>load_data</code> and stores the resulting DataFrame in the cache. Since we&#x27;re using <code>st.cache_resource</code>, it does <strong>not</strong> create a copy but stores the original DataFrame.</li>
<li>Then we drop the column <code>&quot;Lat&quot;</code> from the DataFrame. Note that this is dropping the column from the <em>original</em> DataFrame stored in the cache. We are manipulating it!</li>
<li>On the second run, Streamlit returns that exact same manipulated DataFrame from the cache. It does not have the column <code>&quot;Lat&quot;</code> anymore! So our call to <code>df.drop</code> results in an exception. Pandas cannot drop a column that doesn&#x27;t exist.</li>
</ul>
<p>The copying behavior of <code>st.cache_data</code> prevents this kind of mutation error. Mutations can only affect a specific copy and not the underlying object in the cache. The next rerun will get its own, unmutated copy of the DataFrame. You can try it yourself, just replace <code>st.cache_resource</code> with <code>st.cache_data</code> above, and you&#x27;ll see that everything works.</p>
<p>Because of this copying behavior,Â <code>st.cache_data</code>Â is the recommended way to cache data transforms and computations â€“ anything that returns a serializable object.</p>
<h4 id="concurrency-issues"><a href="/develop/concepts/architecture/caching#concurrency-issues"><span class="icon icon-link"></span></a>Concurrency issues</h4>
<p>Now let&#x27;s look at what can happen when multiple users concurrently mutate an object in the cache. Let&#x27;s say you have a function that returns a list. Again, we are using <code>st.cache_resource</code> to cache it so that we are not creating a copy:</p>
<section class="code_Container__pq3Nr"><div class="code_Pre__3lyyf"><code class="language-python">@st.cache_resource
def create_list():
    l = [1, 2, 3]
    return l

l = create_list()
first_list_value = l[0]
l[0] = first_list_value + 1

st.write(&quot;l[0] is:&quot;, l[0])
</code></div></section>
<p>Let&#x27;s say user A runs the app. They will see the following output:</p>
<section class="code_Container__pq3Nr"><div class="code_Pre__3lyyf"><code class="language-python">l[0] is: 2
</code></div></section>
<p>Let&#x27;s say another user, B, visits the app right after. In contrast to user A, they will see the following output:</p>
<section class="code_Container__pq3Nr"><div class="code_Pre__3lyyf"><code class="language-python">l[0] is: 3
</code></div></section>
<p>Now, user A reruns the app immediately after user B. They will see the following output:</p>
<section class="code_Container__pq3Nr"><div class="code_Pre__3lyyf"><code class="language-python">l[0] is: 4
</code></div></section>
<p>What is happening here? Why are all outputs different?</p>
<ul>
<li>When user A visits the app,Â <code>create_list()</code>Â is called, and the listÂ <code>[1, 2, 3]</code>Â is stored in the cache. This list is then returned to user A. The first value of the list, <code>1</code>, is assigned to <code>first_list_value</code> , and <code>l[0]</code>Â is changed to <code>2</code>.</li>
<li>When user B visits the app,Â <code>create_list()</code>Â returns the mutated list from the cache:Â <code>[2, 2, 3]</code>. The first value of the list, <code>2</code>, is assigned to <code>first_list_value</code> and <code>l[0]</code>Â is changed to <code>3</code>.</li>
<li>When user A reruns the app,Â <code>create_list()</code>Â returns the mutated list again:Â <code>[3, 2, 3]</code>. The first value of the list, <code>3</code>, is assigned to <code>first_list_value,</code> and <code>l[0]</code>Â is changed to 4.</li>
</ul>
<p>If you think about it, this makes sense. Users A and B use the same list object (the one stored in the cache). And since the list object is mutated, user A&#x27;s change to the list object is also reflected in user B&#x27;s app.</p>
<p>This is why you must be careful about mutating objects cached with <code>st.cache_resource</code>, especially when multiple users access the app concurrently. If we had usedÂ <code>st.cache_data</code>Â instead ofÂ <code>st.cache_resource</code>, the app would have copied the list object for each user, and the above example would have worked as expected â€“ users A and B would have both seen:</p>
<section class="code_Container__pq3Nr"><div class="code_Pre__3lyyf"><code class="language-python">l[0] is: 2
</code></div></section>
<section class="callout_Container__TMaoi note_Note__5vxcU"><section class="iconHeader_Container__SQOie"><i class="iconHeader_Icon__o8TXI iconHeader_LightBlueBackground__FLCU8" style="transform:rotate(45deg)">push_pin</i><h4 class="iconHeader_Title__7VTtg iconHeader_LightBlueForeground__GNqzz">Note</h4></section><p>This toy example might seem benign. But data corruption can be extremely dangerous! Imagine we had worked with the financial records of a large bank here. You surely don&#x27;t want to wake up with less money on your account just because someone used the wrong caching decorator ðŸ˜‰</p></section>
<a name="migrating-from-stcache" class="headerLink_HashLink__wuW0v"></a><h2 class="headerLink_HeaderContainer__RZUrb group"><a href="/develop/concepts/architecture/caching#migrating-from-stcache"><span class="icon icon-link"></span></a>Migrating from st.cache<div class="headerLink_CopyLink__GJbCz"><svg width="14" height="17" viewBox="0 0 14 17" fill="none" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><path fill-rule="evenodd" clip-rule="evenodd" d="M10.7548 0.0313721C10.7051 0.0194702 10.6571 0.00793457 10.609 0H9.87278C9.83686 8.09808L4.43217 7.27759C4.46809 7.25977 4.46809 7.18842 4.46809 7.15271C4.41421 6.59979 4.57582 6.11816 4.97085 5.72577L8.54405 2.17615L9.13659 1.58752C9.76504 0.998901 10.7167 0.998901 11.3452 1.58752C12.0095 2.21179 12.0095 3.2464 11.3452 3.90637L7.25123 7.97327C6.8562 8.36566 6.38936 8.54401 5.83273 8.49054C5.77885 8.47266 5.72499 8.47272 5.68908 8.50836L4.86311 9.32886C4.95289 9.36456 5.00676 9.40021 5.06062 9.41803C6.15593 9.81049 7.17941 9.66779 8.02333 8.84729C9.45979 7.45599 10.8783 6.06464 12.2609 4.6377C13.7333 3.12152 12.9971 0.606445 10.9501 0.0713501C10.8805 0.0614624 10.8164 0.0461426 10.7548 0.0313721ZM7.34082 7.47388C7.62811 7.2063 7.9154 6.9209 8.20269 6.6355C8.18016 6.62988 8.16114 6.62427 8.14401 6.6192C8.10655 6.60822 8.07805 6.59985 8.04109 6.59985C7.03556 6.15393 5.83253 6.3501 5.04246 7.11713C3.606 8.52625 2.1875 9.93542 0.768994 11.3624C0.14053 11.9867 -0.0928837 12.7715 0.032803 13.6277C0.194409 14.7515 0.840817 15.5184 1.9002 15.8752C2.97755 16.2319 3.94717 16.0001 4.75517 15.2152C5.6766 14.3118 6.59005 13.4004 7.50616 12.4864C7.96467 12.0289 8.42384 11.5708 8.88501 11.1127C9.56733 10.4348 9.81871 9.61432 9.67506 8.66895C9.63916 8.41925 9.56733 8.16949 9.42369 7.9198C9.13639 8.2052 8.8491 8.47272 8.57975 8.75812C8.54385 8.776 8.54385 8.84735 8.54385 8.90082C8.61567 9.41809 8.47203 9.8819 8.09495 10.2565C6.71235 11.6478 5.31181 13.0391 3.91125 14.4125C3.51623 14.8228 2.99551 14.9655 2.43889 14.8406C1.81042 14.6979 1.4154 14.3234 1.23584 13.7347C1.05629 13.1282 1.19993 12.5753 1.64882 12.1294C2.34011 11.4337 3.03141 10.747 3.72271 10.0603C4.41401 9.37354 5.10531 8.68677 5.79661 7.99115C6.17369 7.59869 6.65849 7.45599 7.19717 7.50952C7.25103 7.50952 7.3049 7.50952 7.34082 7.47388Z" fill="#808495"></path></svg></div></h2>
<p>We introduced the caching commands described above in Streamlit 1.18.0. Before that, we had one catch-all command <code>st.cache</code>. Using it was often confusing, resulted in weird exceptions, and was slow. That&#x27;s why we replaced <code>st.cache</code> with the new commands in 1.18.0 (read more in this <a href="https://blog.streamlit.io/introducing-two-new-caching-commands-to-replace-st-cache/">blog post</a>). The new commands provide a more intuitive and efficient way to cache your data and resources and are intended to replace <code>st.cache</code> in all new development.</p>
<p>If your app is still using <code>st.cache</code>, don&#x27;t despair! Here are a few notes on migrating:</p>
<ul>
<li>Streamlit will show a deprecation warning if your app uses <code>st.cache</code>.</li>
<li>We will not remove <code>st.cache</code> soon, so you don&#x27;t need to worry about your 2-year-old app breaking. But we encourage you to try the new commands going forward â€“ they will be way less annoying!</li>
<li>Switching code to the new commands should be easy in most cases. To decide whether to use <code>st.cache_data</code> or <code>st.cache_resource</code>, read <a href="/develop/concepts/architecture/caching#deciding-which-caching-decorator-to-use">Deciding which caching decorator to use</a>. Streamlit will also recognize common use cases and show hints right in the deprecation warnings.</li>
<li>Most parameters from <code>st.cache</code> are also present in the new commands, with a few exceptions:<!-- -->
<ul>
<li><code>allow_output_mutation</code> does not exist anymore. You can safely delete it. Just make sure you use the right caching command for your use case.</li>
<li><code>suppress_st_warning</code> does not exist anymore. You can safely delete it. Cached functions can now contain Streamlit commands and will replay them. If you want to use widgets inside cached functions, set <code>experimental_allow_widgets=True</code>. See <a href="/develop/concepts/architecture/caching#input-widgets">Input widgets</a> for an example.</li>
</ul>
</li>
</ul>
<p>If you have any questions or issues during the migration process, please contact us on the <a href="https://discuss.streamlit.io/">forum</a>, and we will be happy to assist you. ðŸŽˆ</p><section class="arrowLinkContainer_Container__QwLgW"><a class="not-link group iconLink_Link__qHAvu" target="_self" href="/develop/concepts/architecture/app-chrome"><i class="iconLink_Icon__Qdy_b">arrow_back</i><span class="iconLink_Truncate__ZFSBK"><span class="arrowLink_Text__Xu0t4">Previous: </span>The app chrome</span></a><a class="not-link group iconLink_Link__qHAvu" target="_self" href="/develop/concepts/architecture/session-state"><i class="iconLink_Icon__Qdy_b arrowLink_NextIcon__btU_f">arrow_forward</i><span class="iconLink_Truncate__ZFSBK"><span class="arrowLink_Text__Xu0t4">Next: </span>Session State</span></a></section><section class="psa_Container__YutqA"><i class="psa_Icon__7ImKM">forum</i><article><h3 class="psa_Title__7EKIa">Still have questions?</h3><p class="psa_Text__mBnWO">Our<!-- --> <a href="https://discuss.streamlit.io" target="_blank" class="psa_Link__cbXKJ">forums</a> <!-- -->are full of helpful information and Streamlit experts.</p></article></section></div></article></section><footer class="footer_Container__r6lKu"><section class="footer_InnerContainer__9_p3M"><hr class="footer_Separator__TSG4w"/><nav class="footer_Navigation__zXrVS"><a class="

It creates a new copy of the data at each function call, making it safe against \", _jsx(_components.a, {\n          href: \"#mutation-and-concurrency-issues\",\n          children: \"mutations and race conditions\"\n        }), \". Using it, you can share these resources across all reruns and sessions of an app without copying or duplication. There is one! So it retrieves the cached object, deserializes it to a DataFrame, and returns it instead of re-running the function and downloading the data again.\"]\n      }), \"\\n\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"This process of serializing and deserializing the cached object creates a copy of our original DataFrame. While this copying behavior may seem unnecessary, it's what we want when caching data objects since it effectively prevents mutation and concurrency issues. Read the section â€œ\", _jsx(_components.a, {\n        href: \"#mutation-and-concurrency-issues\",\n        children: \"Mutation and concurrency issues\"\n      }), \"\\\" below to understand this in more detail.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(Warning, {\n      children: _jsxs(_components.p, {\n        children: [_jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"st.cache_data\"\n        }), \" implicitly uses the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"pickle\"\n        }), \" module, which is known to be insecure. Anything your cached function returns is pickled and stored, then unpickled on retrieval. Ensure your cached functions return trusted values because it is possible to construct malicious pickle data that will execute arbitrary code during unpickling. Never load data that could have come from an untrusted source in an unsafe mode or that could have been tampered with. \", _jsx(_components.strong, {\n          children: \"Only load data you trust\"\n        }), \".\"]\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h4, {\n      id: \"examples\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#examples\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Examples\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(\"br\", {}), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.strong, {\n        children: \"DataFrame transformations\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"In the example above, we already showed how to cache loading a DataFrame. It can also be useful to cache DataFrame transformations such as \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"df.filter\"\n      }), \", \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"df.apply\"\n      }), \", or \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"df.sort_values\"\n      }), \". Especially with large DataFrames, these operations can be slow.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"@st.cache_data\\ndef transform(df):\\n    df = df.filter(items=['one', 'three'])\\n    df = df.apply(np.sum, axis=0)\\n\\treturn df\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.strong, {\n        children: \"Array computations\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"Similarly, it can make sense to cache computations on NumPy arrays:\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"@st.cache_data\\ndef add(arr1, arr2):\\n\\treturn arr1 + arr2\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.strong, {\n        children: \"Database queries\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"You usually make SQL queries to load data into your app when working with databases. Repeatedly running these queries can be slow, cost money, and degrade the performance of your database. We strongly recommend caching any database queries in your app. See also \", _jsx(_components.a, {\n        href: \"/develop/tutorials/databases\",\n        children: \"our guides on connecting Streamlit to different databases\"\n      }), \" for in-depth examples.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"connection = database.connect()\\n\\n@st.cache_data\\ndef query():\\n    return pd.read_sql_query(\\\"SELECT * from table\\\", connection)\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(Tip, {\n      children: _jsxs(_components.p, {\n        children: [\"You should set a \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"ttl\"\n        }), \" (time to live) to get new results from your database. If you set \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"st.cache_data(ttl=3600)\"\n        }), \", Streamlit invalidates any cached values after 1 hour (3600 seconds) and runs the cached function again. See details in \", _jsx(_components.a, {\n          href: \"#controlling-cache-size-and-duration\",\n          children: \"Controlling cache size and duration\"\n        }), \".\"]\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.strong, {\n        children: \"API calls\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"Similarly, it makes sense to cache API calls. Doing so also avoids rate limits.\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"@st.cache_data\\ndef api_call():\\n    response = requests.get('https://jsonplaceholder.typicode.com/posts/1')\\n    return response.json()\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.strong, {\n        children: \"Running ML models (inference)\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"Running complex machine learning models can use significant time and memory. To avoid rerunning the same computations over and over, use caching.\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"@st.cache_data\\ndef run_model(inputs):\\n    return model(inputs)\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h3, {\n      id: \"stcache_resource\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#stcache_resource\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"st.cache_resource\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [_jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n      }), \" is the right command to cache â€œresources\\\" that should be available globally across all users, sessions, and reruns. It has more limited use cases than \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_data\"\n      }), \", especially for caching database connections and ML models. Within each user session, an \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"@st.cache_resource\"\n      }), \"-decorated function returns the cached instance of the return value (if the value is already cached). Therefore, objects cached by \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n      }), \" act like singletons and can mutate.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h4, {\n      id: \"usage-1\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#usage-1\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Usage\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"As an example for \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n      }), \", let's look at a typical machine learning app. As a first step, we need to load an ML model. We do this with \", _jsx(_components.a, {\n        href: \"https://huggingface.co/docs/transformers/index\",\n        children: \"Hugging Face's transformers library\"\n      }), \":\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"from transformers import pipeline\\nmodel = pipeline(\\\"sentiment-analysis\\\")  # ðŸ‘ˆ Load the model\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"If we put this code into a Streamlit app directly, the app will load the model at each rerun or user interaction. Repeatedly loading the model poses two problems:\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.ul, {\n      children: [\"\\n\", _jsx(_components.li, {\n        children: \"Loading the model takes time and slows down the app.\"\n      }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.li, {\n        children: \"Each session loads the model from scratch, which takes up a huge amount of memory.\"\n      }), \"\\n\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Instead, it would make much more sense to load the model once and use that same object across all users and sessions. That's exactly the use case for \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n      }), \"! Let's add it to our app and process some text the user entered:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"from transformers import pipeline\\n\\n@st.cache_resource  # ðŸ‘ˆ Add the caching decorator\\ndef load_model():\\n    return pipeline(\\\"sentiment-analysis\\\")\\n\\nmodel = load_model()\\n\\nquery = st.text_input(\\\"Your query\\\", value=\\\"I love Streamlit! ðŸŽˆ\\\")\\nif query:\\n    result = model(query)[0]  # ðŸ‘ˆ Classify the query text\\n    st.write(result)\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"If you run this app, you'll see that the app calls \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"load_model\"\n      }), \" only once â€“ right when the app starts. Subsequent runs will reuse that same model stored in the cache, saving time and memory!\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h4, {\n      id: \"behavior-1\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#behavior-1\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Behavior\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(\"br\", {}), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Using \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n      }), \" is very similar to using \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_data\"\n      }), \". But there are a few important differences in behavior:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.ul, {\n      children: [\"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.li, {\n        children: [\"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n          children: [_jsx(_components.code, {\n            children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n          }), \" does \", _jsx(_components.strong, {\n            children: \"not\"\n          }), \" create a copy of the cached return value but instead stores the object itself in the cache. All mutations on the function's return value directly affect the object in the cache, so you must ensure that mutations from multiple sessions do not cause problems. In short, the return value must be thread-safe.\"]\n        }), \"\\n\", _jsx(Warning, {\n          children: _jsxs(_components.p, {\n            children: [\"Using \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n              children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n            }), \" on objects that are not thread-safe might lead to crashes or corrupted data. Learn more below under \", _jsx(_components.a, {\n              href: \"#mutation-and-concurrency-issues\",\n              children: \"Mutation and concurrency issues\"\n            }), \".\"]\n          })\n        }), \"\\n\"]\n      }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.li, {\n        children: [\"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n          children: [\"Not creating a copy means there's just one global instance of the cached return object, which saves memory, e.g. when using a large ML model. In computer science terms, we create a \", _jsx(_components.a, {\n            href: \"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Singleton_pattern\",\n            children: \"singleton\"\n          }), \".\"]\n        }), \"\\n\"]\n      }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.li, {\n        children: [\"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n          children: [\"Return values of functions do not need to be serializable. This behavior is great for types not serializable by nature, e.g., database connections, file handles, or threads. Caching these objects with \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n            children: \"st.cache_data\"\n          }), \" is not possible.\"]\n        }), \"\\n\"]\n      }), \"\\n\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h4, {\n      id: \"examples-1\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#examples-1\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Examples\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(\"br\", {}), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.strong, {\n        children: \"Database connections\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [_jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n      }), \" is useful for connecting to databases. Usually, you're creating a connection object that you want to reuse globally for every query. Creating a new connection object at each run would be inefficient and might lead to connection errors. That's exactly what \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n      }), \" can do, e.g., for a Postgres database:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"@st.cache_resource\\ndef init_connection():\\n    host = \\\"hh-pgsql-public.ebi.ac.uk\\\"\\n    database = \\\"pfmegrnargs\\\"\\n    user = \\\"reader\\\"\\n    password = \\\"NWDMCE5xdipIjRrp\\\"\\n    return psycopg2.connect(host=host, database=database, user=user, password=password)\\n\\nconn = init_connection()\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Of course, you can do the same for any other database. Have a look at \", _jsx(_components.a, {\n        href: \"/develop/tutorials/databases\",\n        children: \"our guides on how to connect Streamlit to databases\"\n      }), \" for in-depth examples.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.strong, {\n        children: \"Loading ML models\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Your app should always cache ML models, so they are not loaded into memory again for every new session. See the \", _jsx(_components.a, {\n        href: \"#usage-1\",\n        children: \"example\"\n      }), \" above for how this works with ðŸ¤—Â Hugging Face models. You can do the same thing for PyTorch, TensorFlow, etc. Here's an example for PyTorch:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"@st.cache_resource\\ndef load_model():\\n    model = torchvision.models.resnet50(weights=ResNet50_Weights.DEFAULT)\\n    model.eval()\\n    return model\\n\\nmodel = load_model()\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h3, {\n      id: \"deciding-which-caching-decorator-to-use\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#deciding-which-caching-decorator-to-use\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Deciding which caching decorator to use\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(\"br\", {}), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"The sections above showed many common examples for each caching decorator. But there are edge cases for which it's less trivial to decide which caching decorator to use. Eventually, it all comes down to the difference between â€œdata\\\" and â€œresource\\\":\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.ul, {\n      children: [\"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.li, {\n        children: [\"Data are serializable objects (objects that can be converted to bytes viaÂ \", _jsx(_components.a, {\n          href: \"https://docs.python.org/3/library/pickle.html\",\n          children: \"pickle\"\n        }), \") that you could easily save to disk. Imagine all the types you would usually store in a database or on a file system â€“ basic types like str, int, and float, but also arrays, DataFrames, images, or combinations of these types (lists, tuples, dicts, and so on).\"]\n      }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.li, {\n        children: \"Resources are unserializable objects that you usually would not save to disk or a database. They are often more complex, non-permanent objects like database connections, ML models, file handles, threads, etc.\"\n      }), \"\\n\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"From the types listed above, it should be obvious that most objects in Python are â€œdata.\\\" That's also why \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_data\"\n      }), \" is the correct command for almost all use cases. \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n      }), \" is a more exotic command that you should only use in specific situations.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"Or if you're lazy and don't want to think too much, look up your use case or return type in the table below ðŸ˜‰:\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.table, {\n      children: [_jsx(_components.thead, {\n        children: _jsxs(_components.tr, {\n          children: [_jsx(_components.th, {\n            align: \"left\",\n  })]\n        }), _jsxs(_components.tr, {\n          children: [_jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"left\",\n            children: \"Querying a database\"\n          }), _jsx(_components.td, })]\n        }), _jsxs(_components.tr, {\n          children: [_jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"left\",\n            children: \"Querying an API\"\n          }), _jsx(_components.td, {\n   })]\n        }), _jsxs(_components.tr, {\n          children: [_jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"left\",\n            children: \"Running an ML model (inference)\"\n          }), _jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"right\",\n            children: \"pandas.DataFrame, str, int, dict, list\"\n          }), _jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"right\",\n            children: \"st.cache_data\"\n          })]\n        }), _jsxs(_components.tr, {\n          children: [_jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"left\",\n            children: \"Creating or children: \"Creating charts\"\n          }), _jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"right\",\n            children: \"matplotlib.figure.Figure, plotly.graph_objects.Figure, altair.Chart\"\n          }), _jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"right\",\n            children: \"st.cache_data (but some libraries require st.cache_resource, since the chart object is not serializable â€“ make     }), _jsxs(_components.tr, {\n          children: [_jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"left\",\n            children: \"Initializing database connections\"\n          }), children: [_jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"left\",\n            children: \"Opening persistent file handles\"\n          }), _jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"right\",\n            children: \"_io.TextIOWrapper\"\n          }), _jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"right\",\n            children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n          })]\n        }), _jsxs(_components.tr, \"right\",\n            children: \"threading.thread\"\n          }), _jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"right\",\n            children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n          })]\n        })]\n      })]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h2, {\n      id: \"advanced-usage\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#advanced-usage\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Advanced usage\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h3, {\n      id: \"controlling-cache-size-and-duration\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#controlling-cache-size-and-duration\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Controlling cache size and duration\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"If your app runs for a long time and constantly caches functions, you might run into two problems:\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.ol, {\n      children: [\"\\n\", _jsx(_components.li, {\n        children: \"The app runs out of memory because the cache is too large.\"\n      }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.li, {\n        children: \"Objects in the cache become stale, e.g. because you cached old data from a database.\"\n      }), \"\\n\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"You can combat these problems with the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"ttl\"\n      }), \" and \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"max_entries\"\n      }), \" parameters, which are available for both caching decorators.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: _jsxs(_components.strong, {\n        children: [\"The \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"ttl\"\n        }), \" (time-to-live) parameter\"]\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [_jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"ttl\"\n      }), \" sets a time to live on a cached function. If that time is up and you call the function again, the app will discard any old, cached values, and the function will be rerun. The newly computed value will then be stored in the cache. This behavior is useful for preventing stale data (problem 2) and the cache from growing too large (problem 1). Especially when pulling data from a database or API, you should always set a \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"ttl\"\n      }), \" so you are not using old data. Here's an example:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"@st.cache_data(ttl=3600)  # ðŸ‘ˆ Cache data for 1 hour (=3600 seconds)\\ndef get_api_data():\\n    data = api.get(...)\\n    return data\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(Tip, {\n      children: _jsxs(_components.p, {\n        children: [\"You can also set \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"ttl\"\n        }), \" values using \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"timedelta\"\n        }), \", e.g., \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"ttl=datetime.timedelta(hours=1)\"\n        }), \".\"]\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: _jsxs(_components.strong, {\n        children: [\"The \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"max_entries\"\n        }), \" parameter\"]\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [_jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"max_entries\"\n      }), \" sets the maximum number of entries in the cache. An upper bound on the number of cache entries is useful for limiting memory (problem 1), especially when caching large objects. The oldest entry will be removed when a new entry is added to a full cache. Here's an example:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"@st.cache_data(max_entries=1000)  # ðŸ‘ˆ Maximum 1000 entries in the cache\\ndef get_large_array(seed):\\n    np.random.seed(seed)\\n    arr = np.random.rand(100000)\\n    return arr\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h3, {\n      id: \"customizing-the-spinner\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#customizing-the-spinner\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Customizing the spinner\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"By default, Streamlit shows a small loading spinner in the app when a cached function is running. You can modify it easily with the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"show_spinner\"\n      }), \" parameter, which is available for both caching decorators:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"@st.cache_data(show_spinner=False)  # ðŸ‘ˆ Disable the spinner\\ndef get_api_data():\\n    data = api.get(...)\\n    return data\\n\\n@st.cache_data(show_spinner=\\\"Fetching data from API...\\\")  # ðŸ‘ˆ Use custom text for spinner\\ndef get_api_data():\\n    data = api.get(...)\\n    return data\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h3, {\n      id: \"excluding-input-parameters\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#excluding-input-parameters\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Excluding input parameters\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"In a cached function, all input parameters must be hashable. Let's quickly explain why and what it means. When the function is called, Streamlit looks at its parameter values to determine if it was cached before. Therefore, it needs a reliable way to compare the parameter values across function calls. Trivial for a string or int â€“ but complex for arbitrary objects! Streamlit uses \", _jsx(_components.a, {\n        href: \"https://en.wikipedia.org/wiki/Hash_function\",\n        children: \"hashing\"\n      }), \" to solve that. It converts the parameter to a stable key and stores that key. At the next function call, it hashes the parameter again and compares it with the stored hash key.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Unfortunately, not all parameters are hashable! E.g., you might pass an unhashable database connection or ML model to your cached function. In this case, you can exclude input parameters from caching. Simply prepend the parameter name with an underscore (e.g., \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"_param1\"\n      }), \"), and it will not be used for caching. Even if it changes, Streamlit will return a cached result if all the other parameters match up.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"Here's an example:\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"@st.cache_data\\ndef fetch_data(_db_connection, num_rows):  # ðŸ‘ˆ Don't hash _db_connection\\n    data = _db_connection.fetch(num_rows)\\n    return data\\n\\nconnection = init_connection()\\nfetch_data(connection, 10)\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"But what if you want to cache a function that takes an unhashable parameter? For example, you might want to cache a function that takes an ML model as input and returns the layer names of that model. Since the model is the only input parameter, you cannot exclude it from caching. In this case you can use the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"hash_funcs\"\n      }), \" parameter to specify a custom hashing function for the model.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h3, {\n      id: \"the-hash_funcs-parameter\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#the-hash_funcs-parameter\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"The \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"hash_funcs\"\n      }), \" parameter\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"As described above, Streamlit's caching decorators hash the input parameters and cached function's signature to determine whether the function has been run before and has a return value stored (\\\"cache hit\\\") or needs to be run (\\\"cache miss\\\"). Input parameters that are not hashable by Streamlit's hashing implementation can be ignored by prepending an underscore to their name. But there two rare cases where this is undesirable. i.e. where you want to hash the parameter that Streamlit is unable to hash:\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.ol, {\n      children: [\"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.li, {\n        children: [\"When Streamlit's hashing mechanism fails to hash a parameter, resulting in a \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"UnhashableParamError\"\n        }), \" being raised.\"]\n      }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.li, {\n        children: \"When you want to override Streamlit's default hashing mechanism for a parameter.\"\n      }), \"\\n\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"Let's discuss each of these cases in turn with examples.\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h4, {\n      id: \"example-1-hashing-a-custom-class\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#example-1-hashing-a-custom-class\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Example 1: Hashing a custom class\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Streamlit does not know how to hash custom classes. If you pass a custom class to a cached function, Streamlit will raise a \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"UnhashableParamError\"\n      }), \". For example, let's define a custom class \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"MyCustomClass\"\n      }), \" that accepts an initial integer score. Let's also define a cached function \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"multiply_score\"\n      }), \" that multiplies the score by a multiplier:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"import streamlit as st\\n\\nclass MyCustomClass:\\n    def __init__(self, initial_score: int):\\n        self.my_score = initial_score\\n\\n@st.cache_data\\ndef multiply_score(obj: MyCustomClass, multiplier: int) -\u003e int:\\n    return obj.my_score * multiplier\\n\\ninitial_score = st.number_input(\\\"Enter initial score\\\", value=15)\\n\\nscore = MyCustomClass(initial_score)\\nmultiplier = 2\\n\\nst.write(multiply_score(score, multiplier))\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"If you run this app, you'll see that Streamlit raises a \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"UnhashableParamError\"\n      }), \" since it does not know how to hash \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"MyCustomClass\"\n      }), \":\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"UnhashableParamError: Cannot hash argument 'obj' (of type __main__.MyCustomClass) in 'multiply_score'.\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"To fix this, we can use the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"hash_funcs\"\n      }), \" parameter to tell Streamlit how to hash \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"MyCustomClass\"\n      }), \". We do this by passing a dictionary to \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"hash_funcs\"\n      }), \" that maps the name of the parameter to a hash function. The choice of hash function is up to the developer. In this case, let's define a custom hash function \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"hash_func\"\n      }), \" that takes the custom class as input and returns the score. We want the score to be the unique identifier of the object, so we can use it to deterministically hash the object:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"import streamlit as st\\n\\nclass MyCustomClass:\\n    def __init__(self, initial_score: int):\\n        self.my_score = initial_score\\n\\ndef hash_func(obj: MyCustomClass) -\u003e int:\\n    return obj.my_score  # or any other value that uniquely identifies the object\\n\\n@st.cache_data(hash_funcs={MyCustomClass: hash_func})\\ndef multiply_score(obj: MyCustomClass, multiplier: int) -\u003e int:\\n    return obj.my_score * multiplier\\n\\ninitial_score = st.number_input(\\\"Enter initial score\\\", value=15)\\n\\nscore = MyCustomClass(initial_score)\\nmultiplier = 2\\n\\nst.write(multiply_score(score, multiplier))\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Now if you run the app, you'll see that Streamlit no longer raises a \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"UnhashableParamError\"\n      }), \" and the app runs as expected.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Let's now consider the case where \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"multiply_score\"\n      }), \" is an attribute of \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"MyCustomClass\"\n      }), \" and we want to hash the entire object:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"import streamlit as st\\n\\nclass MyCustomClass:\\n    def __init__(self, initial_score: int):\\n        self.my_score = initial_score\\n\\n    @st.cache_data\\n    def multiply_score(self, multiplier: int) -\u003e int:\\n        return self.my_score * multiplier\\n\\ninitial_score = st.number_input(\\\"Enter initial score\\\", value=15)\\n\\nscore = MyCustomClass(initial_score)\\nmultiplier = 2\\n\\nst.write(score.multiply_score(multiplier))\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"If you run this app, you'll see that Streamlit raises a \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"UnhashableParamError\"\n      }), \" since it cannot hash the argument \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"'self' (of type __main__.MyCustomClass) in 'multiply_score'\"\n      }), \". A simple fix here could be to use Python's \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"hash()\"\n      }), \" function to hash the object:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"import streamlit as st\\n\\nclass MyCustomClass:\\n    def __init__(self, initial_score: int):\\n        self.my_score = initial_score\\n\\n    @st.cache_data(hash_funcs={\\\"__main__.MyCustomClass\\\": lambda x: hash(x.my_score)})\\n    def multiply_score(self, multiplier: int) -\u003e int:\\n        return self.my_score * multiplier\\n\\ninitial_score = st.number_input(\\\"Enter initial score\\\", value=15)\\n\\nscore = MyCustomClass(initial_score)\\nmultiplier = 2\\n\\nst.write(score.multiply_score(multiplier))\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Above, the hash function is defined as \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"lambda x: hash(x.my_score)\"\n      }), \". This creates a hash based on the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"my_score\"\n      }), \" attribute of the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"MyCustomClass\"\n      }), \" instance. As long as \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"my_score\"\n      }), \" remains the same, the hash remains the same. Thus, the result of \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"multiply_score\"\n      }), \" can be retrieved from the cache without recomputation.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"As an astute Pythonista, you may have been tempted to use Python's \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"id()\"\n      }), \" function to hash the object like so:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"import streamlit as st\\n\\nclass MyCustomClass:\\n    def __init__(self, initial_score: int):\\n        self.my_score = initial_score\\n\\n    @st.cache_data(hash_funcs={\\\"__main__.MyCustomClass\\\": id})\\n    def multiply_score(self, multiplier: int) -\u003e int:\\n        return self.my_score * multiplier\\n\\ninitial_score = st.number_input(\\\"Enter initial score\\\", value=15)\\n\\nscore = MyCustomClass(initial_score)\\nmultiplier = 2\\n\\nst.write(score.multiply_score(multiplier))\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"If you run the app, you'll notice that Streamlit recomputes \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"multiply_score\"\n      }), \" each time even if \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"my_score\"\n      }), \" hasn't changed! Puzzled? In Python, \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"id()\"\n      }), \" returns the identity of an object, which is unique and constant for the object during its lifetime. This means that even if the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"my_score\"\n      }), \" value is the same between two instances of \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"MyCustomClass\"\n      }), \", \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"id()\"\n      }), \" will return different values for these two instances, leading to different hash values. As a result, Streamlit considers these two different instances as needing separate cached values, thus it recomputes the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"multiply_score\"\n      }), \" each time even if \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"my_score\"\n      }), \" hasn't changed.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"This is why we discourage using it as hash func, and instead encourage functions that return deterministic, true hash values. That said, if you know what you're doing, you can use \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"id()\"\n      }), \" as a hash function. Just be aware of the consequences. For example, \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"id\"\n      }), \" is often the \", _jsx(_components.em, {\n        children: \"correct\"\n      }), \" hash func when you're passing the result of an \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"@st.cache_resource\"\n      }), \" function as the input param to another cached function. There's a whole class of object types that arenâ€™t otherwise hashable.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h4, {\n      id: \"example-2-hashing-a-pydantic-model\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#example-2-hashing-a-pydantic-model\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Example 2: Hashing a Pydantic model\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"Let's consider another example where we want to hash a Pydantic model:\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"import streamlit as st\\nfrom pydantic import BaseModel\\n\\nclass Person(BaseModel):\\n    name: str\\n\\n@st.cache_data\\ndef identity(person: Person):\\n    return person\\n\\nperson = identity(Person(name=\\\"Lee\\\"))\\nst.write(f\\\"The person is {person.name}\\\")\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Above, we define a custom class \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"Person\"\n      }), \" using Pydantic's \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"BaseModel\"\n      }), \" with a single attribute name. We also define an \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"identity\"\n      }), \" function which accepts an instance of \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"Person\"\n      }), \" as an arg and returns it without modification. This function is intended to cache the result, therefore, if called multiple times with the same \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"Person\"\n      }), \" instance, it won't recompute but return the cached instance.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"If you run the app, however, you'll run into a \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"UnhashableParamError: Cannot hash argument 'person' (of type __main__.Person) in 'identity'.\"\n      }), \" error. This is because Streamlit does not know how to hash the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"Person\"\n      }), \" class. To fix this, we can use the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"hash_funcs\"\n      }), \" kwarg to tell Streamlit how to hash \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"Person\"\n      }), \".\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"In the version below, we define a custom hash function \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"hash_func\"\n      }), \" that takes the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"Person\"\n      }), \" instance as input and returns the name attribute. We want the name to be the unique identifier of the object, so we can use it to deterministically hash the object:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"import streamlit as st\\nfrom pydantic import BaseModel\\n\\nclass Person(BaseModel):\\n    name: str\\n\\n@st.cache_data(hash_funcs={Person: lambda p: p.name})\\ndef identity(person: Person):\\n    return person\\n\\nperson = identity(Person(name=\\\"Lee\\\"))\\nst.write(f\\\"The person is {person.name}\\\")\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h4, {\n      id: \"example-3-hashing-a-ml-model\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#example-3-hashing-a-ml-model\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Example 3: Hashing a ML model\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"There may be cases where you want to pass your favorite machine learning model to a cached function. For example, let's say you want to pass a TensorFlow model to a cached function, based on what model the user selects in the app. You might try something like this:\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"import streamlit as st\\nimport tensorflow as tf\\n\\n@st.cache_resource\\ndef load_base_model(option):\\n    if option == 1:\\n        return tf.keras.applications.ResNet50(include_top=False, weights=\\\"imagenet\\\")\\n    else:\\n        return tf.keras.applications.MobileNetV2(include_top=False, weights=\\\"imagenet\\\")\\n\\n@st.cache_resource\\ndef load_layers(base_model):\\n    return [layer.name for layer in base_model.layers]\\n\\noption = st.radio(\\\"Model 1 or 2\\\", [1, 2])\\n\\nbase_model = load_base_model(option)\\n\\nlayers = load_layers(base_model)\\n\\nst.write(layers)\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"In the above app, the user can select one of two models. Based on the selection, the app loads the corresponding model and passes it to \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"load_layers\"\n      }), \". This function then returns the names of the layers in the model. If you run the app, you'll see that Streamlit raises a \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"UnhashableParamError\"\n      }), \" since it cannot hash the argument \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"'base_model' (of type keras.engine.functional.Functional) in 'load_layers'\"\n      }), \".\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"If you disable hashing for \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"base_model\"\n      }), \" by prepending an underscore to its name, you'll observe that regardless of which base model is chosen, the layers displayed are same. This subtle bug is due to the fact that the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"load_layers\"\n      }), \" function is not re-run when the base model changes. This is because Streamlit does not hash the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"base_model\"\n      }), \" argument, so it does not know that the function needs to be re-run when the base model changes.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"To fix this, we can use the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"hash_funcs\"\n      }), \" kwarg to tell Streamlit how to hash the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"base_model\"\n      }), \" argument. In the version below, we define a custom hash function \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"hash_func\"\n      }), \": \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"Functional: lambda x: x.name\"\n      }), \". Our choice of hash func is informed by our knowledge that the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"name\"\n      }), \" attribute of a \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"Functional\"\n      }), \" object or model uniquely identifies it. As long as the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"name\"\n      }), \" attribute remains the same, the hash remains the same. Thus, the result of \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"load_layers\"\n      }), \" can be retrieved from the cache without recomputation.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"import streamlit as st\\nimport tensorflow as tf\\nfrom keras.engine.functional import Functional\\n\\n@st.cache_resource\\ndef load_base_model(option):\\n    if option == 1:\\n        return tf.keras.applications.ResNet50(include_top=False, weights=\\\"imagenet\\\")\\n    else:\\n        return tf.keras.applications.MobileNetV2(include_top=False, weights=\\\"imagenet\\\")\\n\\n@st.cache_resource(hash_funcs={Functional: lambda x: x.name})\\ndef load_layers(base_model):\\n    return [layer.name for layer in base_model.layers]\\n\\noption = st.radio(\\\"Model 1 or 2\\\", [1, 2])\\n\\nbase_model = load_base_model(option)\\n\\nlayers = load_layers(base_model)\\n\\nst.write(layers)\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"In the above case, we could also have used \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"hash_funcs={Functional: id}\"\n      }), \" as the hash function. This is because \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"id\"\n      }), \" is often the \", _jsx(_components.em, {\n        children: \"correct\"\n      }), \" hash func when you're passing the result of an \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"@st.cache_resource\"\n      }), \" function as the input param to another cached function.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h4, {\n      id: \"example-4-overriding-streamlits-default-hashing-mechanism\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#example-4-overriding-streamlits-default-hashing-mechanism\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Example 4: Overriding Streamlit's default hashing mechanism\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"Let's consider another example where we want to override Streamlit's default hashing mechanism for a pytz-localized datetime object:\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"from datetime import datetime\\nimport pytz\\nimport streamlit as st\\n\\ntz = pytz.timezone(\\\"Europe/Berlin\\\")\\n\\n@st.cache_data\\ndef load_data(dt):\\n    return dt\\n\\nnow = datetime.now()\\nst.text(load_data(dt=now))\\n\\nnow_tz = tz.localize(datetime.now())\\nst.text(load_data(dt=now_tz))\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"It may be surprising to see that although \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"now\"\n      }), \" and \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"now_tz\"\n      }), \" are of the same \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"\u003cclass 'datetime.datetime'\u003e\"\n      }), \" type, Streamlit does not how to hash \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"now_tz\"\n      }), \" and raises a \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"UnhashableParamError\"\n      }), \". In this case, we can override Streamlit's default hashing mechanism for \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"datetime\"\n      }), \" objects by passing a custom hash function to the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"hash_funcs\"\n      }), \" kwarg:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"from datetime import datetime\\n\\nimport pytz\\nimport streamlit as st\\n\\ntz = pytz.timezone(\\\"Europe/Berlin\\\")\\n\\n@st.cache_data(hash_funcs={datetime: lambda x: x.strftime(\\\"%a %d %b %Y, %I:%M%p\\\")})\\ndef load_data(dt):\\n    return dt\\n\\nnow = datetime.now()\\nst.text(load_data(dt=now))\\n\\nnow_tz = tz.localize(datetime.now())\\nst.text(load_data(dt=now_tz))\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"Let's now consider a case where we want to override Streamlit's default hashing mechanism for NumPy arrays. While Streamlit natively hashes Pandas and NumPy objects, there may be cases where you want to override Streamlit's default hashing mechanism for these objects.\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"For example, let's say we create a cache-decorated \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"show_data\"\n      }), \" function that accepts a NumPy array and returns it without modification. In the bellow app, \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"data = df[\\\"str\\\"].unique()\"\n      }), \" (which is a NumPy array) is passed to the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"show_data\"\n      }), \" function.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"import time\\nimport numpy as np\\nimport pandas as pd\\nimport streamlit as st\\n\\n@st.cache_data\\ndef get_data():\\n    df = pd.DataFrame({\\\"num\\\": [112, 112, 2, 3], \\\"str\\\": [\\\"be\\\", \\\"a\\\", \\\"be\\\", \\\"c\\\"]})\\n    return df\\n\\n@st.cache_data\\ndef show_data(data):\\n    time.sleep(2)  # This makes the function take 2s to run\\n    return data\\n\\ndf = get_data()\\ndata = df[\\\"str\\\"].unique()\\n\\nst.dataframe(show_data(data))\\nst.button(\\\"Re-run\\\")\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Since \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"data\"\n      }), \" is always the same, we expect the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"show_data\"\n      }), \" function to return the cached value. However, if you run the app, and click the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"Re-run\"\n      }), \" button, you'll notice that the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"show_data\"\n      }), \" function is re-run each time. We can assume this behavior is a consequence of Streamlit's default hashing mechanism for NumPy arrays.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"To work around this, let's define a custom hash function \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"hash_func\"\n      }), \" that takes a NumPy array as input and returns a string representation of the array:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"import time\\nimport numpy as np\\nimport pandas as pd\\nimport streamlit as st\\n\\n@st.cache_data\\ndef get_data():\\n    df = pd.DataFrame({\\\"num\\\": [112, 112, 2, 3], \\\"str\\\": [\\\"be\\\", \\\"a\\\", \\\"be\\\", \\\"c\\\"]})\\n    return df\\n\\n@st.cache_data(hash_funcs={np.ndarray: str})\\ndef show_data(data):\\n    time.sleep(2)  # This makes the function take 2s to run\\n    return data\\n\\ndf = get_data()\\ndata = df[\\\"str\\\"].unique()\\n\\nst.dataframe(show_data(data))\\nst.button(\\\"Re-run\\\")\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Now if you run the app, and click the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"Re-run\"\n      }), \" button, you'll notice that the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"show_data\"\n      }), \" function is no longer re-run each time. It's important to note here that our choice of hash function was very naive and not necessarily the best choice. For example, if the NumPy array is large, converting it to a string representation may be expensive. In such cases, it is up to you as the developer to define what a good hash function is for your use case.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h4, {\n      id: \"static-elements\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#static-elements\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Static elements\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"Since version 1.16.0, cached functions can contain Streamlit commands! For example, you can do this:\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"@st.cache_data\\ndef get_api_data():\\n    data = api.get(...)\\n    st.success(\\\"Fetched data from API!\\\")  # ðŸ‘ˆ Show a success message\\n    return data\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"As we know, Streamlit only runs this function if it hasn't been cached before. On this first run, the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.success\"\n      }), \" message will appear in the app. But what happens on subsequent runs? It still shows up! Streamlit realizes that there is an \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.\"\n      }), \" command inside the cached function, saves it during the first run, and replays it on subsequent runs. Replaying static elements works for both caching decorators.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"You can also use this functionality to cache entire parts of your UI:\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"@st.cache_data\\ndef show_data():\\n    st.header(\\\"Data analysis\\\")\\n    data = api.get(...)\\n    st.success(\\\"Fetched data from API!\\\")\\n    st.write(\\\"Here is a plot of the data:\\\")\\n    st.line_chart(data)\\n    st.write(\\\"And here is the raw data:\\\")\\n    st.dataframe(data)\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h4, {\n      id: \"input-widgets\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#input-widgets\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Input widgets\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"You can also use \", _jsx(_components.a, {\n        href: \"/develop/api-reference/widgets\",\n        children: \"interactive input widgets\"\n      }), \" like \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.slider\"\n      }), \" or \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.text_input\"\n      }), \" in cached functions. Widget replay is an experimental feature at the moment. To enable it, you need to set the \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"experimental_allow_widgets\"\n      }), \" parameter:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"@st.cache_data(experimental_allow_widgets=True)  # ðŸ‘ˆ Set the parameter\\ndef get_data():\\n    num_rows = st.slider(\\\"Number of rows to get\\\")  # ðŸ‘ˆ Add a slider\\n    data = api.get(..., num_rows)\\n    return data\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"Streamlit treats the slider like an additional input parameter to the cached function. If you change the slider position, Streamlit will see if it has already cached the function for this slider value. If yes, it will return the cached value. If not, it will rerun the function using the new slider value.\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Using widgets in cached functions is extremely powerful because it lets you cache entire parts of your app. But it can be dangerous! Since Streamlit treats the widget value as an additional input parameter, it can easily lead to excessive memory usage. Imagine your cached function has five sliders and returns a 100 MB DataFrame. Then we'll add 100 MB to the cache for \", _jsx(_components.em, {\n        children: \"every permutation\"\n      }), \" of these five slider values â€“ even if the sliders do not influence the returned data! These additions can make your cache explode very quickly. Please be aware of this limitation if you use widgets in cached functions. We recommend using this feature only for isolated parts of your UI where the widgets directly influence the cached return value.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(Warning, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.p, {\n        children: \"Support for widgets in cached functions is experimental. We may change or remove it anytime without warning. Please use it with care!\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(Note, {\n      children: _jsxs(_components.p, {\n        children: [\"Two widgets are currently not supported in cached functions: \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"st.file_uploader\"\n        }), \" and \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"st.camera_input\"\n        }), \". We may support them in the future. Feel free to \", _jsx(_components.a, {\n          href: \"https://github.com/streamlit/streamlit/issues\",\n          children: \"open a GitHub issue\"\n        }), \" if you need them!\"]\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h3, {\n      id: \"dealing-with-large-data\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#dealing-with-large-data\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Dealing with large data\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"As we explained, you should cache data objects with \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_data\"\n      }), \". But this can be slow for extremely large data, e.g., DataFrames or arrays with \u003e100 million rows. That's because of the \", _jsx(_components.a, {\n        href: \"#copying-behavior\",\n        children: \"copying behavior\"\n      }), \" of \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_data\"\n      }), \": on the first run, it serializes the return value to bytes and deserializes it on subsequent runs. Both operations take time.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"If you're dealing with extremely large data, it can make sense to use \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n      }), \" instead. It does not create a copy of the return value via serialization/deserialization and is almost instant. But watch out: any mutation to the function's return value (such as dropping a column from a DataFrame or setting a value in an array) directly manipulates the object in the cache. You must ensure this doesn't corrupt your data or lead to crashes. See the section on \", _jsx(_components.a, {\n        href: \"#mutation-and-concurrency-issues\",\n        children: \"Mutation and concurrency issues\"\n      }), \" below.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"When benchmarking \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_data\"\n      }), \" on pandas DataFrames with four columns, we found that it becomes slow when going beyond 100 million rows. The table shows runtimes for both caching decorators at different numbers of rows (all with four columns):\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.table, {\n      children: [_jsx(_components.thead, {\n        children: _jsxs(_components.tr, {\n          children: [_jsx(_components.th, {}), _jsx(_components.th, {}), _jsx(_components.th, {\n            align: \"center\",\n            children: \"10M }), _jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"center\",\n            children: \"0 s\"\n          }), _jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"center\",\n            children: \"0 s\"\n          }), _jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"center\",\n            children: \"0 s\"\n          }), _jsx(_components.td, {\n            align: \"center\",\n            children: \"0 s\"\n
