{\n            align: \"left\",\n            children: _jsx(_components.em, {\n              children: \"*For the first run, the table only shows the overhead time of using the caching decorator. It does not include the runtime of the cached function itself.\"\n            })\n          })\n        })\n      })]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h3, {\n      id: \"mutation-and-concurrency-issues\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#mutation-and-concurrency-issues\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Mutation and concurrency issues\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"In the sections above, we talked a lot about issues when mutating return objects of cached functions. This topic is complicated! But it's central to understanding the behavior differences between \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_data\"\n      }), \" and \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n      }), \". So let's dive in a bit deeper.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"First, we should clearly define what we mean by mutations and concurrency:\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.ul, {\n      children: [\"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.li, {\n        children: [\"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n          children: [\"By \", _jsx(_components.strong, {\n            children: \"mutations\"\n          }), \", we mean any changes made to a cached function's return value \", _jsx(_components.em, {\n            children: \"after\"\n          }), \" that function has been called. I.e. something like this:\"]\n        }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n          children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n            className: \"language-python\",\n            children: \"@st.cache_data\\ndef create_list():\\n    l = [1, 2, 3]\\n\\nl = create_list()  # ðŸ‘ˆ Call the function\\nl[0] = 2  # ðŸ‘ˆ Mutate its return value\\n\"\n          })\n        }), \"\\n\"]\n      }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.li, {\n        children: [\"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n          children: [\"By \", _jsx(_components.strong, {\n            children: \"concurrency\"\n          }), \", we mean that multiple sessions can cause these mutations at the same time. Streamlit is a web framework that needs to handle many users and sessions connecting to an app. If two people view an app at the same time, they will both cause the Python script to rerun, which may manipulate cached return objects at the same time â€“ concurrently.\"]\n        }), \"\\n\"]\n      }), \"\\n\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Mutating cached return objects can be dangerous. It can lead to exceptions in your app and even corrupt your data (which can be worse than a crashed app!). Below, we'll first explain the copying behavior of \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_data\"\n      }), \" and show how it can avoid mutation issues. Then, we'll show how concurrent mutations can lead to data corruption and how to prevent it.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h4, {\n      id: \"copying-behavior\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#copying-behavior\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Copying behavior\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [_jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_data\"\n      }), \" creates a copy of the cached return value each time the function is called. This avoids most mutations and concurrency issues. To understand it in detail, let's go back to the \", _jsx(_components.a, {\n        href: \"#usage\",\n        children: \"Uber ridesharing example\"\n      }), \" from the section on \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_data\"\n      }), \" above. We are making two modifications to it:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.ol, {\n      children: [\"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.li, {\n        children: [\"We are using \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n        }), \" instead of \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"st.cache_data\"\n        }), \". \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n        }), \" does \", _jsx(_components.strong, {\n          children: \"not\"\n        }), \" create a copy of the cached object, so we can see what happens without the copying behavior.\"]\n      }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.li, {\n        children: [\"After loading the data, we manipulate the returned DataFrame (in place!) by dropping the column \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"\\\"Lat\\\"\"\n        }), \".\"]\n      }), \"\\n\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"Here's the code:\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"@st.cache_resource   # ðŸ‘ˆ Turn off copying behavior\\ndef load_data(url):\\n    df = pd.read_csv(url)\\n    return df\\n\\ndf = load_data(\\\"https://raw.githubusercontent.com/plotly/datasets/master/uber-rides-data1.csv\\\")\\nst.dataframe(df)\\n\\ndf.drop(columns=['Lat'], inplace=True)  # ðŸ‘ˆ Mutate the dataframe inplace\\n\\nst.button(\\\"Rerun\\\")\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Let's run it and see what happens! The first run should work fine. But in the second run, you see an exception: \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"KeyError: \\\"['Lat'] not found in axis\\\"\"\n      }), \". Why is that happening? Let's go step by step:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.ul, {\n      children: [\"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.li, {\n        children: [\"On the first run, Streamlit runs \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"load_data\"\n        }), \" and stores the resulting DataFrame in the cache. Since we're using \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n        }), \", it does \", _jsx(_components.strong, {\n          children: \"not\"\n        }), \" create a copy but stores the original DataFrame.\"]\n      }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.li, {\n        children: [\"Then we drop the column \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"\\\"Lat\\\"\"\n        }), \" from the DataFrame. Note that this is dropping the column from the \", _jsx(_components.em, {\n          children: \"original\"\n        }), \" DataFrame stored in the cache. We are manipulating it!\"]\n      }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.li, {\n        children: [\"On the second run, Streamlit returns that exact same manipulated DataFrame from the cache. It does not have the column \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"\\\"Lat\\\"\"\n        }), \" anymore! So our call to \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"df.drop\"\n        }), \" results in an exception. Pandas cannot drop a column that doesn't exist.\"]\n      }), \"\\n\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"The copying behavior of \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_data\"\n      }), \" prevents this kind of mutation error. Mutations can only affect a specific copy and not the underlying object in the cache. The next rerun will get its own, unmutated copy of the DataFrame. You can try it yourself, just replace \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n      }), \" with \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_data\"\n      }), \" above, and you'll see that everything works.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Because of this copying behavior,Â \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_data\"\n      }), \"Â is the recommended way to cache data transforms and computations â€“ anything that returns a serializable object.\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.h4, {\n      id: \"concurrency-issues\",\n      children: [_jsx(_components.a, {\n        \"aria-hidden\": \"true\",\n        tabIndex: \"-1\",\n        href: \"#concurrency-issues\",\n        children: _jsx(_components.span, {\n          className: \"icon icon-link\"\n        })\n      }), \"Concurrency issues\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.p, {\n      children: [\"Now let's look at what can happen when multiple users concurrently mutate an object in the cache. Let's say you have a function that returns a list. Again, we are using \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n        children: \"st.cache_resource\"\n      }), \" to cache it so that we are not creating a copy:\"]\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"@st.cache_resource\\ndef create_list():\\n    l = [1, 2, 3]\\n    return l\\n\\nl = create_list()\\nfirst_list_value = l[0]\\nl[0] = first_list_value + 1\\n\\nst.write(\\\"l[0] is:\\\", l[0])\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"Let's say user A runs the app. They will see the following output:\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"l[0] is: 2\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"Let's say another user, B, visits the app right after. In contrast to user A, they will see the following output:\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"l[0] is: 3\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"Now, user A reruns the app immediately after user B. They will see the following output:\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.pre, {\n      children: _jsx(_components.code, {\n        className: \"language-python\",\n        children: \"l[0] is: 4\\n\"\n      })\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsx(_components.p, {\n      children: \"What is happening here? Why are all outputs different?\"\n    }), \"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.ul, {\n      children: [\"\\n\", _jsxs(_components.li, {\n        children: [\"When user A visits the app,Â \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"create_list()\"\n        }), \"Â is called, and the listÂ \", _jsx(_components.code, {\n          children: \"[1, 2, 3]\"\n        }), \"Â is stored in the cache.
